### [A Brief Taxonomy of Online Anti-Georgism](https://www.progress.org/articles/a-brief-taxonomy-of-online-anti-georgism/)
- **illustrates** [`objections/search-theoretic-critique`](https://progress.org/wiki/search-theoretic-critique/) — anchor: **“resource rent is needed to incentivize discovery”**
  - page's claim: Land rent rewards costly discovery, so taxing it kills production
  - sentence: …For example, Gochenour and Caplans paper on how resource rent is needed to incentivize discovery in natural resources is frequently brought up in online arguments.…
  - why: the essay directly cites the search-theoretic critique's core claim as a recurring anti-Georgist argument
- **counters** [`objections/land-cannot-be-assessed`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-cannot-be-assessed/) — anchor: **“multiple jurisdictions around the world and across history have managed to assess land just fine”**
  - page's claim: Land value cannot be accurately separated from improvement value
  - sentence: …That multiple jurisdictions around the world and across history have managed to assess land just fine is quietly ignored.…
  - why: the essay dismisses the assessment-denial objection by pointing to empirical evidence that land assessment works in practice
- **illustrates** [`objections/taxing-quasi-rents-kills-innovation`](https://progress.org/wiki/taxing-quasi-rents-kills-innovation/) — anchor: **“pursuit of monopoly rents is a powerful driver of innovation”**
  - page's claim: Taxing above-normal returns kills the incentive to innovate
  - sentence: …In his telling, the pursuit of monopoly rents is a powerful driver of innovation and conditions of truly competitive profit are a recipe for stagnation and anti-social behavior.…
  - why: the essay presents Thiel's Schumpeterian argument that monopoly rents drive innovation, which is the core of the quasi-rent objection

### [A Georgist Approach to Emissions Rights](https://www.progress.org/articles/a-georgist-approach-to-emissions-rights/)
- **supports** [`narratives/ecological-rent`](https://progress.org/wiki/ecological-rent/) — anchor: **“unpaid takings of common natural wealth”** ⚠️ *ungrounded anchor*
  - page's claim: Pollution and extraction are unpaid takings of common natural wealth.
  - sentence: …The environmental extension of the Georgist principle: pollution and extraction are unpaid takings of common natural wealth, and charging rent for them — capped carbon, resource ro…
  - why: The essay argues that emitting greenhouse gasses without paying for the atmosphere's absorption capacity is an unpaid taking of a scarce common natural resource, directly supporting the ecological ren
- **supports** [`benefits/carbon-pricing-cuts-emissions`](https://progress.org/wiki/carbon-pricing-cuts-emissions/) — anchor: **“raising the cost of emitting”**
  - page's claim: Pricing the right to emit reduces emissions without wrecking growth.
  - sentence: …International climate negotiations aim to gradually shift the economic burden from future generations to the present generation, by raising the cost of emitting.…
  - why: The essay supports the claim that pricing emissions (raising the cost of emitting) is the mechanism to distribute atmospheric rents justly, aligning with the carbon pricing claim.
- **supports** [`narratives/citizens-dividend-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/citizens-dividend-narrative/) — anchor: **“let everyone in the community have an equal share”**
  - page's claim: Rent from common wealth should be paid out equally to everyone.
  - sentence: …George’s approach is to socialize the natural resource rents and let everyone in the community have an equal share of them.…
  - why: The essay explicitly endorses the Georgist approach of socializing natural resource rents (atmospheric rents) and distributing them equally, which is the core of the citizens dividend narrative.

### [A German State Quietly Implemented a Land Value Tax](https://www.progress.org/articles/a-german-state-quietly-implemented-a-land-value-tax/)
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-not-widely-adopted`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-not-widely-adopted/) — anchor: **“land value taxes are not politically impossible”**
  - page's claim: If LVT is so good, why has no one adopted it?
  - sentence: …The experience is still young and the tax rate still small, but it sets a precedent: land value taxes are not politically impossible.…
  - why: The essay directly answers the revealed-preference objection by presenting Baden-Württemberg as a major industrial economy that successfully adopted LVT.
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-reduces-sprawl`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-reduces-sprawl/) — anchor: **“gives an incentive to be careful with the scarce resource of land”**
  - page's claim: Land value taxation reduces urban sprawl
  - sentence: …The Green Party found it very appealing because the land value tax is a tax which gives an incentive to be careful with the scarce resource of land.…
  - why: The essay provides evidence for the anti-sprawl claim by citing the Green Party's rationale for adopting LVT to encourage land efficiency and compact development.
- **illustrates** [`benefits/split-rate-increases-construction`](https://progress.org/wiki/split-rate-increases-construction/) — anchor: **“a split-rate structure”**
  - page's claim: Split-rate taxation increases urban construction
  - sentence: …Baden-Württemberg chose to tax land alone but built in one notable political accommodation: a split-rate structure.…
  - why: The essay illustrates the real-world application of a split-rate tax structure, showing how it is implemented in a major economy.

### [A Just and Practicable Income Tax](https://www.progress.org/articles/a-just-and-practicable-income-tax/)
- **supports** [`narratives/tax-land-not-labor`](https://progress.org/wiki/tax-land-not-labor/) — anchor: **“tax upon the income of accumulated wealth alone”**
  - page's claim: Taxes should fall on land, not on labor.
  - sentence: …Since, then, new revenue must be had, since no further extension of protective duties, if such were possible, and no mere reduction of duties now imposed would produce the needed revenue, and since nine-tenths of all existing Federal taxes …
  - why: the essay argues that existing taxes fall on labor and should be replaced by a tax on accumulated wealth (unearned income), directly supporting the Georgist claim that taxation should shift off labor.
- **supports** [`benefits/landlords-cannot-pass-lvt-to-tenants`](https://progress.org/wiki/landlords-cannot-pass-lvt-to-tenants/) — anchor: **“all indirect taxation, without any exception whatever, and under any conceivable system, is grossly unequal and unjust”**
  - page's claim: Land taxes cannot be shifted to tenants.
  - sentence: …Thus all indirect taxation, without any exception whatever, and under any conceivable system, is grossly unequal and unjust.…
  - why: the essay contrasts indirect taxes (which burden the poor) with direct taxes on accumulated wealth, supporting the Georgist distinction that direct land-value taxes are not shifted like indirect consu
- **illustrates** [`narratives/single-tax-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/single-tax-narrative/) — anchor: **“a tax upon the income of accumulated wealth alone”**
  - page's claim: One levy on land values can replace other taxes.
  - sentence: …Since, then, new revenue must be had, since no further extension of protective duties, if such were possible, and no mere reduction of duties now imposed would produce the needed revenue, and since nine-tenths of all existing Federal taxes …
  - why: the essay presents the Shearman/George proposal to replace taxes on labor with a single tax on unearned income from accumulated wealth, illustrating the single-tax narrative.

  - why: The essay directly proposes shifting all taxes off wages onto unearned income, echoing the single-tax platform's core principle of taxing rent rather than labor.
- **supports** [`narratives/tax-land-not-labor`](https://progress.org/wiki/tax-land-not-labor/) — anchor: **“not on wages”**
  - page's claim: Shift taxation off wages and investment onto land and rent.
  - sentence: …All taxes needed to regulate the monetary system are to fall on unearned income and large estates, not on wages, with the understanding that a corporation's net income/profits (along with the dividends paid out from those profits) are also …
  - why: The platform explicitly removes taxes from wages and places them on unearned income, aligning with the Georgist principle of taxing land and rent rather than labor.
- **supports** [`problems/corporate-profits-increasingly-rents`](https://progress.org/wiki/corporate-profits-increasingly-rents/) — anchor: **“a corporation's net income/profits (along with the dividends paid out from those profits) are also unearned income”**
  - page's claim: Corporate profits increasingly reflect economic rents rather than competitive returns.
  - sentence: …All taxes needed to regulate the monetary system are to fall on unearned income and large estates, not on wages, with the understanding that a corporation's net income/profits (along with the dividends paid out from those profits) are also …
  - why: By classifying corporate profits and dividends as unearned income, the essay engages the claim that corporate profits are rents rather than returns to production.

### [A More Prosperous Vancouver](https://www.progress.org/articles/a-more-prosperous-vancouver/)

- **supports** [`problems/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land/) — anchor: **“the city invests in additional infrastructure near your property, your land becomes more valuable”**
  - page's claim: Public infrastructure investment raises nearby land values.
  - sentence: …Take, for example, urban land: if you buy a property, and then the city invests in additional infrastructure near your property, your land becomes more valuable — even if you haven’t invested a penny into further developing that property.…
  - why: The sentence provides a direct example of public investment capitalizing into land value, explicitly engaging the page's claim.
- **supports** [`narratives/the-rentier-economy`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-rentier-economy/) — anchor: **“This phenomenon underpins most of our modern economy, and it even has a name: Rentier Capitalism”**

  - why: The sentence explicitly identifies the capture of community-created land value by private sellers as rentier capitalism, engaging the page's narrative.

### [About Interest](https://www.progress.org/articles/about-interest/)

  - sentence: …The cheap credit generates real estate booms that end in a financial crisis and depression when land values become unaffordable, and, as the money stops expanding, when interest rates go back up.…
  - why: The sentence asserts that artificially cheap credit fuels real estate booms that culminate in financial crisis, directly supporting the land-speculation-causes-cycles claim.

  - why: The sentence states that cheap credit disproportionately channels into real estate borrowing, supporting the claim that banking/credit growth is tied to land.
- **supports** [`problems/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land/) — anchor: **“Public goods make locations more attractive and productive, increasing land rent and land values”**

  - why: The sentence directly asserts that public goods capitalize into higher land rent and values, matching the claim.

### [AFFEERCE Georgism (part 2)](https://www.progress.org/articles/affeerce-georgism-part-2/)

  - sentence: …Land was seized from indigenous populations and often from each other.…
  - why: The essay directly asserts the historical origin of land titles as violent seizure, aligning with the narrative that current ownership stems from dispossession.
- **illustrates** [`narratives/citizens-dividend-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/citizens-dividend-narrative/) — anchor: **“every person receives a $370 housing distribution”**
  - page's claim: Rent from land and natural resources is common property paid out equally.
  - sentence: …Because every person receives a $370 housing distribution, which can be used for ground rent, apartment rent, mortgages, utilities and renovations, I estimate that 95% of the population will pay nothing of their own money for rent.…
  - why: The essay provides a concrete implementation of distributing collected ground rent equally to all citizens, illustrating the citizen's dividend concept.
- **supports** [`problems/speculative-vacancy-wastes-cities`](https://progress.org/wiki/speculative-vacancy-wastes-cities/) — anchor: **“In the inner city, slums are impossible”**
  - page's claim: Land underuse and speculative vacancy persist in high-demand cities.
  - sentence: …This leads to a second conclusion: In the inner city, slums are impossible.…
  - why: The essay argues that the 'trebling' mechanism forces efficient land use by penalizing low ground rents, directly addressing the problem of land underuse in high-demand areas.

### [Affordable Housing](https://www.progress.org/articles/affordable-housing/)
- **supports** [`benefits/landlords-cannot-pass-lvt-to-tenants`](https://progress.org/wiki/landlords-cannot-pass-lvt-to-tenants/) — anchor: **“property rental market will simply accommodate the tenant”**

  - why: The sentence argues that competitive rental markets prevent landlords from shifting land contributions onto tenants, directly supporting the claim that LVT cannot be passed on.
- **supports** [`benefits/rent-dividends-reduce-poverty`](https://progress.org/wiki/rent-dividends-reduce-poverty/) — anchor: **“financed entirely from community land contributions”**
  - page's claim: Rent dividends reduce poverty and inequality.
  - sentence: …One effective way to do this is through the issuance of a partial Universal Basic Income to all residents, financed entirely from community land contributions.…
  - why: The sentence proposes a rent-funded dividend as the mechanism to prevent gentrification and share rising rents with all residents, directly supporting the claim that rent dividends reduce poverty.
- **supports** [`problems/homelessness-is-housing-cost-problem`](https://progress.org/wiki/homelessness-is-housing-cost-problem/) — anchor: **“the homeless are not only homeless—they are landless”**
  - page's claim: Homelessness is fundamentally a housing-cost problem.
  - sentence: …Land belongs to the people, yet the homeless are not only homeless—they are landless.…
  - why: The sentence reframes homelessness as a lack of access to land rather than individual failings, directly supporting the claim that homelessness is driven by housing and land costs.

  - page's claim: Shift taxation off labor and investment onto land and pollution.

  - why: The essay advocates the green tax shift — off income/sales taxes and onto pollution and land value — which is the core of the tax-land-not-labor narrative.
- **supports** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“taking back the value generated by beneficial public works and civic services”**
  - page's claim: Public works and civic services generate land value, recoverable for public use.
  - sentence: …The tapping of land rent for public revenue has no excess burden and prevents the subsidy of land by taking back the value generated by beneficial public works and civic services.…
  - why: The essay states that land value is generated by public works and civic services and should be taken back, asserting the community-creates-land-value claim.

  - sentence: …In 1983, British economist Fred Harrison published his seminal book The Power in the Land, in which he analyzed the economic history of Great Britain since 1701 and noted that property prices—driven by increases in underlying land values—te…

- **supports** [`problems/high-land-rents-suppress-productivity`](https://progress.org/wiki/high-land-rents-suppress-productivity/) — anchor: **“the expensive price of land has consequences that reverberate through the entire economy”**
  - page's claim: High land costs restrict economic production and cause depressions.
  - sentence: …Because the cost of land—and therefore the cost of location—directly affects people’s abilities to interact and connect with one another in the context of society, the expensive price of land has consequences that reverberate through the en…
  - why: The sentence explicitly argues that high land prices restrict wealth production across the economy, aligning with the claim that land rents suppress productivity.
- **supports** [`problems/speculative-vacancy-wastes-cities`](https://progress.org/wiki/speculative-vacancy-wastes-cities/) — anchor: **“withhold land from use and public enjoyment in expectation of future gains”**

  - why: The sentence describes how speculative withholding of land constricts supply to drive up prices, directly supporting the claim about speculative vacancy.

  - page's claim: Homevoters block land value taxation politically
  - sentence: …Homevoters ended Pittsburgh’s split rate system.…
  - why: The essay directly cites homevoters' political power as the reason LVT is not adopted, confirming the objection's mechanism.
- **counters** [`objections/lvt-not-widely-adopted`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-not-widely-adopted/) — anchor: **“misses the very real examples of Georgist policy that already exist today”**
  - page's claim: If LVT is so good, why hasn't it been adopted?
  - sentence: …While it’s true we’ve never seen policy like that in the U.S., this view is reductive and misses the very real examples of Georgist policy that already exist today.…
  - why: The essay argues against the claim that Georgism hasn't been tried by pointing to existing land-leasing implementations.
- **illustrates** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“mechanisms for capturing unexpected upside”**
  - page's claim: Public investment and community create land value
  - sentence: …Though the land is priced against current expectations, there are mechanisms for capturing unexpected upside.…
  - why: The lease structures described capture land-value increases created by community and public action, illustrating the narrative's core mechanism.

  - why: the sentence explicitly identifies the root cause of economic injustice as the theft of land, directly supporting the claim that land titles descend from enclosure and dispossession.

- **supports** [`problems/finance-growth-is-land-credit`](https://progress.org/wiki/finance-growth-is-land-credit/) — anchor: **“none of that higher land value belongs in a mortgage”**
  - page's claim: Banking growth is largely mortgage credit against land.
  - sentence: …However, none of that higher land value belongs in a mortgage.…
  - why: The essay argues that land value should not be mortgaged, engaging the claim that mortgage credit is largely against land.

### [Is a Sales Tax Voluntary?](https://www.progress.org/articles/is-a-sales-tax-voluntary/)
- **supports** [`benefits/landlords-cannot-pass-lvt-to-tenants`](https://progress.org/wiki/landlords-cannot-pass-lvt-to-tenants/) — anchor: **“land does not shrink, hide, or flee when taxed”**
  - page's claim: Land value tax incidence falls on landowners, not tenants.
  - sentence: …By taxing rent indirectly, the sales tax imposes a deadweight loss, whereas if the rent had been taxed directly, there is no deadweight loss, since land does not shrink, hide, or flee when taxed.…
  - why: the essay asserts the fixed-supply mechanism that prevents deadweight loss and tax-shifting under direct land taxation
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss/) — anchor: **“the sales tax imposes a deadweight loss”**
  - page's claim: Shifting tax from capital to land raises welfare without deadweight loss.
  - sentence: …By taxing rent indirectly, the sales tax imposes a deadweight loss, whereas if the rent had been taxed directly, there is no deadweight loss, since land does not shrink, hide, or flee when taxed.…
  - why: the essay contrasts the deadweight loss of indirect taxation with the efficiency of taxing land rent directly
- **supports** [`narratives/tax-land-not-labor`](https://progress.org/wiki/tax-land-not-labor/) — anchor: **“the taxes should be on the consumption of land, valued by its rent”**
  - page's claim: Tax land rather than labor, sales, or consumption.
  - sentence: …The taxation of spatial service based on the rent of land does not reduce the land, so if consumption taxes there must be, logically the taxes should be on the consumption of land, valued by its rent.…
  - why: the essay concludes that if any consumption tax is warranted, it should fall on land rent rather than goods or labor

  - why: The sentence asserts that the business cycle is driven by land rent dynamics, directly supporting the claim page's thesis that land speculation causes cycles.

### [Kinetic Rent and Potential Rent](https://www.progress.org/articles/kinetic-rent-and-potential-rent/)
- **supports** [`problems/high-land-rents-suppress-productivity`](https://progress.org/wiki/high-land-rents-suppress-productivity/) — anchor: **“less productive land shifts”**
  - page's claim: High land rents suppress productivity
  - sentence: …The potential rent is unknown, since even if the deadweight loss from taxation can be estimated, the quanta losses due to less productive land shifts is unknown.…
  - why: The essay argues that taxes convert kinetic rent to potential rent by forcing land to less productive uses, directly supporting the claim that land-use misallocation suppresses productivity.
- **supports** [`problems/land-rent-could-fund-government`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-rent-could-fund-government/) — anchor: **“estimate the total amount of rent that could be collected for public revenue”**
  - page's claim: Land rent could fund a large share of government
  - sentence: …If we seek to estimate the total amount of rent that could be collected for public revenue, we need to include both the potential and the kinetic rent.…
  - why: The essay asserts that total rent available for public revenue exceeds measured kinetic rent because potential rent is currently suppressed by deadweight-loss taxation.
- **supports** [`problems/public-goods-fundable-from-land-rent`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-goods-fundable-from-land-rent/) — anchor: **“Paying for public goods from rent does not reduce that value”**
  - page's claim: Public goods can be funded from the land rent they create
  - sentence: …Paying for public goods from rent does not reduce that value, the rent, but it does reduce the purchase price of land, as the title holder receives less net rent.…
  - why: The essay directly engages the Henry George theorem by arguing that funding public goods from land rent preserves the rent's value, unlike taxing wages or profits.

### [Land Rent as a Tax](https://www.progress.org/articles/land-rent-as-a-tax/)

  - sentence: …The only way to avoid rent as taxation is to avoid the excessive land speculation by collecting the land rent and distributing it as either cash or public goods.…
  - why: The sentence supports the claim by prescribing the collection and distribution of land rent to fund public goods as the solution to speculative rent taxation.

### [Letter From a Young Distributist](https://www.progress.org/articles/letter-from-a-young-distributist/)
- **supports** [`narratives/single-tax-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/single-tax-narrative/) — anchor: **“taxation and equal distribution of land and natural resources, alongside the abolition of taxes on labor and capital”**

  - sentence: …In response, George formulated an economic system based on the taxation and equal distribution of land and natural resources, alongside the abolition of taxes on labor and capital- a virtual common ownership of the Earth.…
  - why: The sentence directly articulates the single tax narrative by describing George's system as taxing land to abolish taxes on labor and capital.
- **supports** [`narratives/citizens-dividend-narrative`](https://progress.org/wiki/citizens-dividend-narrative/) — anchor: **“giving the money back to each family”** ⚠️ *ungrounded anchor*
  - page's claim: Rent from land and natural resources is common property paid out equally.
  - sentence: …This consists of enacting a tax on the value of land not counting improvements, and then using that money for both government expenses and a citizen’s dividend which gives the money back to each family.…
  - why: The sentence explicitly describes the citizen's dividend as distributing collected land rent back equally to families, embodying the common wealth dividend narrative.
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-improves-housing-affordability`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-improves-housing-affordability/) — anchor: **“lowering its sale price, to a theoretical value of zero”**
  - page's claim: Land value taxation lowers land prices to improve affordability.
  - sentence: …These policies would widely distribute land - the distributist ideal - by lowering its sale price, to a theoretical value of zero with a full tax.…
  - why: The sentence asserts that a land value tax lowers land prices (down to zero under a full tax), directly engaging the claim that LVT improves affordability via tax capitalization.

  - sentence: …Justice requires that this ground rent be divided among the people equally, either for public goods or as an individual basic income.…
  - why: The essay asserts that ground rent should be distributed equally, including as a basic income, which is the citizens' dividend claim.
- **supports** [`narratives/community-creates-land-value`](https://progress.org/wiki/community-creates-land-value/) — anchor: **“generation of land rent from the public goods”**
  - page's claim: Public goods and community generate land rent.
  - sentence: …The mother of all subsidies is the generation of land rent from the public goods and welfare provided by government.…
  - why: The essay explicitly states that land rent is generated by public goods, which is the community-creates-land-value claim.

  - why: The sentence asserts that public works and civic services increase land rent and land value, directly engaging the claim that public investment capitalizes into land values.

  - page's claim: Speculative vacancy persists in high-demand cities
  - sentence: …And finally, productive land use is penalized & speculation is rewarded , with vacant land enjoying relatively low tax bills and are penalized with a sharp increase in taxes if they choose to develop.…
  - why: the essay provides a specific NYC example of how the property tax system rewards speculative vacancy, illustrating the claim that underuse persists in high-demand cities.
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-improves-housing-affordability`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-improves-housing-affordability/) — anchor: **“reducing or removing taxes on building values, offsetting lost revenues with a land value tax”**
  - page's claim: Land value taxation can improve housing affordability
  - sentence: …More comprehensively, we propose offering a carrot to developers by reducing or removing taxes on building values, offsetting lost revenues with a land value tax .…
  - why: the essay proposes LVT as a mechanism to improve housing affordability by encouraging development, directly supporting the claim that LVT improves affordability.

### [The Modern Georgism of Respected Economists Part 1/3: Joseph Stiglitz](https://www.progress.org/articles/the-modern-georgism-of-respected-economists-part-1-3-joseph-stiglitz/)

  - sentence: …Stiglitz himself supports both halves of the synthesis that lies at the heart of Georgist tax policy: taxing as many resource rents as we can while untaxing productive things like labor.…
  - why: the sentence asserts Stiglitz endorses the Georgist policy of taxing resource rents while untaxing labor
- **supports** [`problems/capital-share-rise-is-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/capital-share-rise-is-land/) — anchor: **“the distinction between true capital and spurious capital”**

  - why: the sentence asserts that Piketty's anomalies are explained by recognizing that what is measured as capital includes land and other non-capital assets

  - why: The sentence explicitly asserts that land value is a product of community and social development rather than individual owner effort, directly supporting the narrative's core claim.

  - why: The essay describes the exact mechanism of speculative vacancy—holding land idle to capture future value increases—which the claim page documents as a persistent problem in high-demand cities.

  - why: the essay argues removing taxes on output/income and taxing land instead avoids stifling production, aligning with the claim that replacing capital taxes with LVT has no efficiency loss.

  - why: the essay directly argues that land value is created by the community and public presence, not by individual owners, which is the core narrative claim

  - why: The essay resolves the asset-rich/cash-poor concern by proposing net-loss compensation, ensuring owners are not forced out if tax burdens exceed their gains.

  - page's claim: Community and public goods create land value
  - sentence: …The typical landowner has been receiving an implicit subsidy from the government, as public goods generate higher rent and land value.…
  - why: The essay asserts that public goods create land value, supporting the narrative that community-generated rent should be recovered for public use.

### [Valence in Economics](https://www.progress.org/articles/valence-in-economics/)
- **supports** [`benefits/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss`](https://progress.org/wiki/lvt-can-replace-capital-taxes-without-efficiency-loss/) — anchor: **“A land-value tax that replaces taxes on transactions would optimize the valence of all factors”**
  - page's claim: Shifting tax from capital to land raises welfare without deadweight loss.
  - sentence: …A land-value tax that replaces taxes on transactions would optimize the valence of all factors.…
  - why: The essay argues that replacing transaction taxes with LVT optimizes factor complementarity, echoing the claim that shifting taxes to land removes efficiency losses.
- **supports** [`problems/speculative-vacancy-wastes-cities`](https://progress.org/wiki/speculative-vacancy-wastes-cities/) — anchor: **“stuck in low-valence uses such as vacant lots”**
  - page's claim: Land underuse and speculative vacancy persist in high-demand cities.
  - sentence: …Much real estate is then stuck in low-valence uses such as vacant lots or one-story buildings in a neighborhood of taller buildings while the land value appreciates.…
  - why: The sentence describes land being held in underused/vacant states while its value appreciates, directly illustrating the claim.
- **supports** [`narratives/tax-land-not-labor`](https://progress.org/wiki/tax-land-not-labor/) — anchor: **“landowners are subsidized as public goods are mostly financed from taxes on labor”**
  - page's claim: Shift taxation off wages and investment onto land.
  - sentence: …In effect, landowners are subsidized as public goods are mostly financed from taxes on labor, while the civic services increase land rent and land value.…
  - why: The sentence critiques taxing labor to fund public goods that benefit land, supporting the narrative to tax land instead of labor.

  - sentence: …Access to public parks and lakes capitalizes directly into land values, and home buyers compete fiercely for properties within the zone of a high-performing school .…
  - why: The essay provides specific examples of public goods (parks, schools) capitalizing into land values, directly supporting the page's claim.
- **illustrates** [`objections/homevoters-will-block-lvt`](https://progress.org/wiki/homevoters-will-block-lvt/) — anchor: **“homevoters ’ can create a scarcity of housing which boosts the value of their own land”**
  - page's claim: Homevoters block development to protect their land values.
  - sentence: …However, by lobbying for strict zoning on their neighbors’ properties, so-called ‘ homevoters ’ can create a scarcity of housing which boosts the value of their own land.…
  - why: The essay illustrates the homevoter mechanism by describing how homeowners lobby for zoning to boost their land values, which is the political economy the page describes.

  - why: The essay argues that shifting taxes off labour and capital onto land avoids the economic drag of taxing productive activity, supporting the claim that LVT replaces capital taxes without efficiency lo

  - why: The essay directly invokes the Henry George Theorem to assert that public spending raises land values, supporting the claim that public investment capitalizes into land.

### [Why Research Farmland Ownership And Values? Part 1](https://www.progress.org/articles/why-research-farmland-ownership-and-values-presented-paper-excerpt-1/)
- **counters** [`objections/land-cannot-be-assessed`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-cannot-be-assessed/) — anchor: **“refute by demonstration the claim that valuation is impracticable”**

  - sentence: …For any government to place values on land, whatever the ostensible purpose, is to provide the infrastructure prerequisite to taxing it, and to refute by demonstration the claim that valuation is impracticable.…
  - why: the essay directly argues that government land valuation programs demonstrate the practicability of assessing land value.
- **counters** [`objections/land-is-just-capital`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-is-just-capital/) — anchor: **“erase the distinction between land and capital”**
  - page's claim: Land is just a form of capital with no economic distinction.
  - sentence: …There is irony in making this point here in the shadow of The Midway because Frank Knight, the granddaddy of Chicago economists, took great pains to destroy the concept of turnover and its reciprocal, the period of investment, and thus to e…
  - why: the essay identifies Frank Knight's attempt to erase the land-capital distinction as something the essay's audience recognizes as false.
- **supports** [`narratives/the-tax-you-cant-dodge`](https://progress.org/wiki/the-tax-you-cant-dodge/) — anchor: **“land is the oldest tax base”**
  - page's claim: Land is a tax base that cannot be hidden or evaded.
  - sentence: …Certainly, at any rate, land is the oldest tax base, and we keep coming back to it even after Howard Jarvis and all that.…
  - why: the essay supports the narrative that land is a uniquely durable and unavoidable tax base by noting its persistent use.

### [Why Research Farmland Ownership And Values? Part 2](https://www.progress.org/articles/why-research-farmland-ownership-and-values-presented-paper-excerpt-2/)
- **supports** [`narratives/land-speculation-causes-cycles`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-speculation-causes-cycles/) — anchor: **“same cause producing banking collapses”**
  - page's claim: Credit-financed land speculation drives recurrent booms and busts.
  - sentence: …Hoyt found the same cause producing banking collapses also in 1837, 1857, 1873, and 1893.…
  - why: The sentence provides historical evidence that land-value cycles caused repeated banking collapses, directly supporting the claim that land speculation drives boom-bust cycles.
- **supports** [`problems/finance-growth-is-land-credit`](https://progress.org/wiki/finance-growth-is-land-credit/) — anchor: **“most of what banks have been monetizing in recent years is not federal debt at all but, rather -- real estate”**
  - page's claim: Modern banking expansion is largely mortgage credit against land.
  - sentence: …Now as defaults accelerate and the system starts to crumble, we suddenly become aware that most of what banks have been monetizing in recent years is not federal debt at all but, rather -- real estate!…
  - why: The sentence asserts that bank credit expansion has been driven by real estate lending, directly supporting the claim that banking growth is largely mortgage credit against land.
- **counters** [`objections/stock-crash-caused-great-depression`](https://progress.org/wiki/stock-crash-caused-great-depression/) — anchor: **“banking collapse was an echo of the real estate collapse”**
  - page's claim: The 1929 stock crash caused the Great Depression.
  - sentence: …In 1933 Professor Herbert D. Simpson of Northwestern University told the American Economic Association that the banking collapse was an echo of the real estate collapse, and there was none to deny what none could hide, much as some wanted t…
  - why: The sentence counters the stock-crash narrative by arguing the banking collapse stemmed from a real estate collapse, not the 1929 stock crash.

### [Why Research Farmland Ownership And Values? Part 3](https://www.progress.org/articles/why-research-farmland-ownership-and-values-presented-paper-excerpt-3/)
- **supports** [`narratives/land-speculation-causes-cycles`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-speculation-causes-cycles/) — anchor: **“there was a land value cycle whose amplitude”**
  - page's claim: Credit-financed land speculation drives boom-bust cycles
  - sentence: …Here we learn that there was a land value cycle whose amplitude, in the appropriate relative terms, far exceeds that of any other cycle of comparable weight.…
  - why: the essay cites Homer Hoyt's historical data to assert that land value cycles dominate other economic cycles, supporting the Georgist claim that land speculation drives boom and bust.
- **supports** [`problems/finance-growth-is-land-credit`](https://progress.org/wiki/finance-growth-is-land-credit/) — anchor: **“increasing credit financing of land purchases”**
  - page's claim: Banking growth is largely mortgage credit against land
  - sentence: …Hoyt also documents a social-psychological process of increasing credit financing of land purchases, and monetization of land value collateral, during the upswing of a cycle.…
  - why: the essay documents how credit expansion during land upswings is tied to land collateral, supporting the claim that banking growth is largely mortgage credit against land.
- **supports** [`problems/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land`](https://progress.org/wiki/public-investment-capitalizes-into-land/) — anchor: **“enhancement and sustenance of land values”**
  - page's claim: Public investment capitalizes into nearby land values
  - sentence: …The main payoff from many public works is their enhancement and sustenance of land values.…
  - why: the essay asserts that public works primarily pay off through land value enhancement, directly supporting the claim that public investment capitalizes into land values.

### [Why Research Farmland Ownership And Values? Part 5](https://www.progress.org/articles/why-research-farmland-ownership-and-values-presented-paper-excerpt-5/)
- **supports** [`objections/land-cannot-be-assessed`](https://progress.org/wiki/land-cannot-be-assessed/) — anchor: **“comparable sales and capitalized income and historical cost, when applied to different properties, do not provide fair assessments”**

### [Why the Crash of 2008 was not a Market Failure](https://www.progress.org/articles/why-the-crash-of-2008-was-not-a-market-failure/)

  - why: the sentence asserts that land-value appreciation triggers speculative demand that drives the boom-bust cycle.
